<t2460>One day, they were almost caught by Ursula.</t2460> <t2461>They had hidden in the barn and were just about to kiss when Ursula came in and innocently turned to Aureliano Jose and asked, "Do you love your aunt very much?"</t2461> <t2462>Aureliano Jose said that he loved her very much.</t2462> <t2463>Ursula, saying "Good for you," measured the flour she had taken out of the sack for bread and returned to the kitchen.</t2463>
<t2464>This event pulled Amaranta out of the madness she had fallen into.</t2464> <t2465>She realized that she had gone too far, that what started as a kissing game with a child had turned into a passion of her later years; that it was dangerous and would lead nowhere, so she abruptly ended it.</t2465> <t2466>At that time, Aureliano Jose, who was about to complete his military training, finally faced reality and started living in the barracks.</t2466> <t2467>On Saturdays, he would go to Catarino's shop with the soldiers.</t2467> <t2468>In his sudden loneliness, his prematurely bursting adolescence, he sought solace in women who smelled of wilted flowers.</t2468> <t2469>He would fit these women into the image in his mind in the dark, straining his imagination to see them as Amaranta.</t2469>
<t2470>Shortly after, conflicting news about the war began to arrive.</t2470> <t2471>On one hand, the government was admitting that the uprising was growing and spreading; on the other hand, the officers in Macondo were receiving secret reports that negotiations should be held immediately and peace should be declared.</t2471> <t2472>In early April, a special envoy arrived for Colonel Gerineldo Marquez.</t2472> <t2473>The envoy confirmed that party leaders had established contact with rebel leaders in the interior of the country and were negotiating a ceasefire agreement in exchange for three ministerial seats for the Liberals, representation of the minority in the House of Representatives, and a general amnesty for rebels who laid down their arms.</t2473> <t2474>The envoy also brought a very secret order from Colonel Aureliano Buendia, who did not accept the terms of the ceasefire.</t2474> <t2475>According to the order, Colonel Gerineldo Marquez was to take his five best men and leave the country.</t2475> <t2476>This order was to be carried out with absolute secrecy.</t2476> <t2477>A week before the announcement of the agreement, when there were conflicting reports from everywhere, Colonel Aureliano Buendia, along with ten trusted officers including Colonel Roque Carnicero, secretly arrived in Macondo after midnight, disbanded the military, buried the weapons, and destroyed the documents.</t2477>
<t2478>Before dawn broke, they left, taking Colonel Gerineldo Marquez and his five men with them.</t2478> <t2479>All of this happened so quickly and secretly that even Ursula only learned of it at the last moment, when someone tapped on her window and whispered, "If you want to see Colonel Aureliano Buendia, come to the door immediately."</t2479> <t2480>Ursula jumped out of bed and rushed to the door in her nightgown.</t2480> <t2481>She could barely make out the horsemen galloping away from the village, leaving a cloud of dust behind them.</t2481> <t2482>She only found out the next day that Aureliano Jose had gone with his father.</t2482>
<t2483>Ten days after the joint declaration by the government and the opposition that the war had ended, news came of Colonel Aureliano Buendia's first armed uprising on the western frontier.</t2483> <t2484>The colonel's numerically small and poorly armed force was repelled in less than a week.</t2484>
<t2485>That year, while the Liberals and Conservatives were placating the public with tales of reconciliation, Colonel Aureliano Buendia launched seven more uprisings.</t2485> <t2486>One night, he shelled Riohacha from a sailing ship.</t2486> <t2487>The soldiers jumped out of their beds and, in retaliation, executed fourteen of the town's leading Liberals.</t2487>
<t2488>Colonel Aureliano Buendia held one of the customs outposts at the border for more than two weeks and called for a general war across the nation.</t2488> <t2489>An expedition he undertook to wage war on the outskirts of the capital resulted in his men disappearing for three months during a frantic effort to clear a path through virgin forests over fifteen hundred kilometers deep.</t2489> <t2490>On one occasion, he approached within twenty kilometers of Macondo and had to retreat to the mountains after encountering government reconnaissance patrols.</t2490> <t2491>He was very close to the place where his father had found the remains of the Spanish galleon years before.</t2491>
<t2492>Visitacion died around that time.</t2492> <t2493>She had given up being a princess in her own tribe out of fear of the insomnia plague, and had attained the happiness of dying a natural death.</t2493> <t2494>She bequeathed that the monthly savings she had accumulated for over twenty years under her bed be unearthed and sent to Colonel Aureliano Buendia so he could continue the war.</t2494> <t2495>However, since news arrived that Colonel Aureliano Buendia had been killed while stationed near the provincial capital, Ursula did not bother to unearth the money.</t2495> <t2496>The government communiqué announcing the colonel's death - the fourth such announcement in the last two years - was taken as fact for up to six months, as there was no news from the colonel.</t2496> <t2497>Just as Ursula and Amaranta were about to add a new mourning to the past ones, unexpected news arrived.</t2497> <t2498>Colonel Aureliano Buendia was alive.</t2498> <t2499>However, he had given up dealing with his own country's government and had joined those working for the federation of other republics in the Caribbean.</t2499>
<t2500>Each time, he appeared under different names and each time in a place a little farther from his country.</t2500> <t2501>It was later learned that his idea at the time was to unite the federalist forces in Central America and to sweep away all conservative regimes from Alaska to Patagonia.</t2501>
<t2502>The first direct news Ursula received from him was a letter sent from the city of Santiago in Cuba a few years after his departure, which reached his mother after passing from hand to hand, yellowing and crumpling along the way.</t2502> <t2503>When Ursula read the letter, she exclaimed, "We have completely lost him."</t2503> <t2504>"At this rate, he will spend Christmas on the other side of the world."</t2504> <t2505>The person to whom Ursula said these words and first showed the letter was Conservative General Jose Raquel Moncada, who had been the mayor of Macondo since the end of the war.</t2505> <t2506>General Moncada expressed his opinion, "It's a pity that this Aureliano is not a Conservative."</t2506>
<t2507>He truly admired her.</t2507> <t2508>Like most conservative civilians, Jose Raquel Moncada had joined the war to defend his party and, despite not being a professional officer, he had earned the title of general due to his usefulness on the battlefield.</t2508> <t2509>However, like most of his colleagues in the party, he was against the war.</t2509> <t2510>He viewed soldiers as idle individuals with no principles, greedy schemers, and experts at intimidating civilians to live in luxury during times of chaos.</t2510> <t2511>Moncada, cultured, intelligent, pleasant, rosy-cheeked, and fond of food and cockfights, was once considered Colonel Aureliano Buendia's most feared rival.</t2511> <t2512>He had managed to establish his own authority over professional officers in the vast region along the coast.</t2512> <t2513>On one occasion, when he was forced to withdraw from a region they held due to strategic circumstances, he left two letters for Colonel Aureliano Buendia.</t2513>
<t2514>In one of the rather long letters, he was calling on the colonel to join the campaign to conduct the war under more humane conditions.</t2514> <t2515>He had written the second letter to his wife, who was in the region dominated by the Liberals, and placed it next to the colonel's letter with the hope that it would be delivered.</t2515> <t2516>From that day on, even during the bloodiest periods of the war, the two commanders would occasionally cease fire and exchange war prisoners.</t2516> <t2517>These ceasefire periods became breathers that brought a certain festive atmosphere, and General Moncada took advantage of these opportunities to teach Colonel Aureliano Buendia how to play chess.</t2517> <t2518>They became good friends.</t2518> <t2519>Gradually, they even planned to unite the beloved and respected elements of both parties, to free the soldiers from the influence of professional politicians, and to establish a humane order that encompassed the best aspects of each doctrine.</t2519> <t2520>After the war, while Colonel Aureliano Buendia was trying to navigate the harsh paths of successive defeats, General Moncada was appointed as a justice of the peace.</t2520>
<t2521>He took off his uniform and put on civilian clothes, replaced the soldiers with unarmed police officers, implemented amnesty laws, and helped the families of a few Liberals who died in the war.</t2521> <t2522>He ensured that Macondo became a district and thus became its first mayor.</t2522> <t2523>And he brought security, peace, and order to the people to such an extent that they thought the war was a meaningless nightmare of the past.</t2523> <t2524>Father Coronel, who had participated in the first federalist war and was nicknamed Bear Fish, replaced Father Nicanor, who died of liver disease.</t2524> <t2525>Bruno Crespi, who married Amparo Moscote and developed his music instruments and toy shop day by day, had a theater built.</t2525> <t2526>Spanish theater companies on tour began to give performances there.</t2526> <t2527>The open-air theater consisted of wooden benches, a stage with velvet curtains adorned with Greek masks, and three ticket booths shaped like lion heads.</t2527> <t2528>Tickets were obtained from the lion's mouth.</t2528>
<t2529>At around this time, the school was also rebuilt.</t2529> <t2530>Don Melchor Escalona, who was brought in from the swampy region, was put in charge of the school.</t2530> <t2531>Escalona made lazy students walk on their knees in the lime-plastered courtyard and filled the mouths of those who talked during class with hot pepper.</t2531> <t2532>The children's parents did not object to these actions.</t2532>
<t2533>The mischievous twins of Santa Sofia de la Piedad, Aureliano Segundo and Jose Arcadio Segundo, were the first students to arrive in class with their slate boards, chalks, and aluminum canteens with their names written on them.</t2533>
<t2534>Remedios, who had inherited her mother's unique beauty, became known as Beautiful Remedios.</t2534> <t2535>Despite time, successive periods of mourning, and a heap of sorrows, Ursula resisted aging.</t2535> <t2536>With the help of Santa Sofia de la Piedad, Ursula accelerated her pastry-making again, and within a few years, not only did she rebuild the fortune her son had squandered in the war, but she also refilled the jars buried in the bedroom with glittering gold.</t2536> <t2537>"As long as God gives me life, there will be no shortage of money in this madhouse," she said.</t2537> <t2538>It was during this time that Aureliano Jose, having fled the federal troops in Nicaragua and signed on as a crew member of a German ship, appeared in the kitchen of the house.</t2538>
<t2539>Aureliano Jose was as strong as a horse, as dark-skinned as a native, and had long hair, and he had secretly decided to marry Amaranta.</t2539> <t2540>When Amaranta saw him come in, she understood why he had come, even though he hadn't said anything yet.</t2540> <t2541>They couldn't look each other in the face at the table.</t2541> <t2542>However, two weeks after his arrival, Aureliano Jose, in front of Ursula, staring into Amaranta's eyes, suddenly said, "I've always thought of you."</t2542> <t2543>Amaranta kept her distance from him, avoided unexpected encounters, and tried to keep Beautiful Remedios by her side.</t2543> <t2544>When her nephew asked her how long she intended to keep the black bandage on her hand, she blushed with shame.</t2544> <t2545>Because she saw this bandage as a symbol of her virginity.</t2545> <t2546>After Aureliano Jose arrived, Amaranta began to bolt the door of her bedroom.</t2546> <t2547>However, hearing the comfortable snores coming from the adjacent room every night, she eventually forgot to bolt the door.</t2547> <t2548>About two months after Aureliano Jose's arrival, one morning Amaranta heard him enter the room.</t2548> <t2549>Then, instead of screaming or running away as she had previously thought she would, she sank into a soft comfort.</t2549>
<t2550>He heard Aureliano José slip under the mosquito net as he always did when he was a child, and when he realized the young man was completely naked, he couldn't stop himself from breaking out in a cold sweat and his teeth chattering.</t2550> <t2551>Breathless with curiosity, he whispered, -Go away, or I'll scream.</t2551> <t2552>However, Aureliano José knew exactly what he had to do.</t2552> <t2553>Because he was no longer a child; he had become a barracks stallion.</t2553> <t2554>That night, the silent and noisy struggles began again and lasted until dawn.</t2554> <t2555>Amaranta, losing herself, said, -I am your aunt.</t2555> <t2556>-I am practically your mother, not just because I am older, but because the only thing I didn't do was breastfeed you; beyond that, I mothered you, she said.</t2556> <t2557>Aureliano would leave at dawn, come back the next morning, and each time he came, he was even more excited by the fact that Amaranta didn't bolt the door.</t2557> <t2558>His desire for her had not diminished for a moment.</t2558>
<t2559>In the dark bedrooms of the occupied cities, in the most wretched of bedrooms, he had found Amaranta, sensed Amaranta in the dried blood smell of the bandages of the wounded, lived Amaranta in the momentary terror of the danger of death, dreamed of her everywhere, all the time.</t2559> <t2560>He had fled from her to forget her; not only going far away but also throwing himself forward with a fury that his comrades called recklessness, yet the more he tried to bury Amaranta's image in the filth of war, the more the war resembled Amaranta.</t2560> <t2561>During his time in hiding, Aureliano Jose had writhed in these pains, seeking ways to kill himself and thus kill the image of Amaranta.</t2561> <t2562>One day, he had listened to a tale from an old man.</t2562> <t2563>In the tale, the man marries his aunt, who is also his uncle's daughter, and in the end, his son becomes his own grandfather.</t2563>
<t2564>Aureliano Jose had escaped from the barracks and come back two weeks after this incident.</t2564> <t2565>He found Amaranta more worn out, more withdrawn, more timid, and curled up at the last corner of maturity than he had imagined, but in the darkness of the bedroom, more passionate than ever, more aggressively defiant in her resistance than ever.</t2565> <t2566>As Amaranta undressed in his hand caresses, she said, "You are a monster."</t2566> <t2567>"You can't do these things to your poor aunt unless you get special permission from the Pope."</t2567> <t2568>Aureliano Jose promised to go to Rome; Amaranta said she would walk across Europe on her knees to kiss the Pope's sandals so that he would lower the drawbridge of the castle.</t2568>
<t2569>Amaranta was protesting, "This doesn't end here."</t2569> <t2570>"If we have a child, it will have a tail like a pig."</t2570>
<t2571>Aureliano Jose paid no attention to these words.</t2571>
<t2572>"Even if you give birth to a thorny lizard, it wouldn't matter," he was saying.</t2572>
<t2573>Aureliano Jose, in the early morning, unable to bear the pain of unrelieved manhood, went to Catarino's shop.</t2573> <t2574>He found a woman with sagging breasts, affectionate and vulgar.</t2574> <t2575>The woman temporarily quenched his hunger.</t2575> <t2576>He also began to try the tactic of disdain towards Amaranta.</t2576> <t2577>He would see Amaranta sitting on the terrace, working at the sewing machine she had quickly mastered, and wouldn't even greet her.</t2577> <t2578>Amaranta compared herself to a boat narrowly escaping crashing into the rocks and couldn't understand why she started thinking about Colonel Gerineldo Marquez, why she nostalgically remembered the days they played Chinese checkers, and why she imagined Gerineldo as the man in her bedroom.</t2578> <t2579>Aureliano Jose, however, did not realize the great defeat he faced the night he could no longer endure the comedy of indifference and returned to Amaranta's room.</t2579> <t2580>Amaranta, with unshakable and unwavering determination, turned him away and bolted her door for life.</t2580>
<t2581>A few months after Aureliano Jose's return, a flamboyant woman, smelling of jasmine, arrived at the door holding the hand of a five-year-old boy.</t2581> <t2582>She said that the boy was the son of Colonel Aureliano Buendia and that she had brought him to Ursula to be baptized.</t2582> <t2583>No one doubted the lineage of the unnamed child: He was the spitting image of the colonel.</t2583> <t2584>It was exactly like the time when Aureliano first saw ice.</t2584> <t2585>The woman described how the child was born: He was born with his eyes wide open.</t2585> <t2586>As soon as he was born, he fixed his eyes, which looked like those of a grown man, on the people around him, as if he were judging them.</t2586> <t2587>His unblinking stare frightened his mother.</t2587>
<t2588>Ursula, "Just like him," she said.</t2588> <t2589>"The only thing missing is that he can't move the chairs with a glance."</t2589>
<t2590>They gave the child the name Aureliano and his mother's surname.</t2590> <t2591>Because according to the laws, until his father officially recognized him, the child could not take his father's surname.</t2591> <t2592>General Moncada became his godfather.</t2592> <t2593>Amaranta insisted a lot that she stay with them to take on the child's upbringing, but the child's mother opposed this.</t2593>
<t2594>Ursula had not yet heard of the custom of sending virgins into the arms of soldiers, just as hens are let loose among roosters.</t2594> <t2595>But she learned it well within that year.</t2595> <t2596>Colonel Aureliano Buendia's nine sons were brought home to be baptized.</t2596> <t2597>The eldest, a dark-skinned, green-eyed boy who did not resemble his father at all, was no more than ten years old.</t2597> <t2598>They kept bringing children of every age and color, but all of them were boys and left no doubt about their paternity.</t2598> <t2599>Among those who came, only two showed distinct characteristics.</t2599> <t2600>One was large for his age and broke every piece of crockery and every pot in the house.</t2600> <t2601>It was as if his hands had the ability to break everything they touched.</t2601> <t2602>The other was a fair-haired boy with light-colored eyes like his mother.</t2602> <t2603>His hair was grown long and curled like a girl's.</t2603> <t2604>He entered the house with a familiarity as if he had been raised there, went straight to the console in Ursula's room, and said, "I want the wind-up ballerina."</t2604>
<t2605>Ursula was taken aback.</t2605> <t2606>She opened the drawer, rummaged through the old, dusty knick-knacks from Melquiades' time, and found the wind-up ballerina wrapped in a pair of socks.</t2606> <t2607>Pietro Crespi had brought it to the house, and then everyone had forgotten about it.</t2607> <t2608>Within less than twelve years, the seventeen sons that the colonel had fathered on his battlefield were baptized with the name Aureliano and their mothers' surnames.</t2608> <t2609>At first, Ursula would fill the pockets of those who came with money, and Amaranta would try to keep them at home.</t2609> <t2610>But eventually, they started to be content with giving them gifts and becoming their godmothers.</t2610> <t2611>Ursula would record the mother's name, address, and the child's place and date of birth in a large ledger, saying, "By baptizing them, we have done our part."</t2611> <t2612>She would say, "We need to keep the records well so that when Aureliano comes, he can make a decision easily."</t2612>
<t2613>While Ursula was discussing this surprising reproduction issue with General Moncada at dinner one day, she hinted that Colonel Aureliano Buendia deeply wished to return one day and gather all his sons at home.</t2613>
<t2614>General Moncada said, "Do not worry, my dear friend, Aureliano will return sooner than you think."</t2614>
<t2615>The truth that General Moncada knew at that moment and did not want to explain was that Colonel Aureliano Buendia was on his way to lead the longest, most relentless, and bloodiest uprising he had ever undertaken until that day.</t2615>
<t2616>The situation became tense again, just like in the months before the first war.</t2616> <t2617>The cockfights, which were held under the protection of the mayor, were suspended.</t2617> <t2618>Captain Aquiles Ricardo, the Garrison Commander, took over the mayoral duties.</t2618> <t2619>The Liberals viewed him as a provocateur.</t2619> <t2620>Ursula said to Aureliano Jose, "Bad things are going to happen."</t2620> <t2621>"Don't go out after six in the evening."</t2621> <t2622>However, no matter how much Ursula pleaded, she couldn't make him listen.</t2622> <t2623>Just as Arcadio once did, Aureliano Jose had also ceased to belong to her.</t2623> <t2624>It seemed that the possibility of living without worrying about daily subsistence, upon returning home, had awakened in him the lazy and profligate tendencies of his uncle, Jose Arcadio.</t2624> <t2625>His passion for Amaranta had passed without leaving a trace.</t2625> <t2626>He wandered aimlessly, played billiards, passed his loneliness with transient women, and plundered the money Ursula had hidden and forgotten.</t2626> <t2627>Eventually, he only stopped by the house to change his clothes.</t2627> <t2628>Ursula complained, "They are all the same."</t2628> <t2629>"At first, their manners and gentlemanliness are impeccable."</t2629> <t2630>"They listen, do whatever they are told, and seem incapable of hurting even an ant."</t2630> <t2631>"But as soon as their beards grow, their morals deteriorate," she grumbled.</t2631>
<t2632>Unlike Arcadio, who never learned who his real parents were, Aureliano Jose found out that he was the son of Pilar Ternera.</t2632> <t2633>The woman had prepared a hammock for him to take his afternoon naps in her house.</t2633> <t2634>Beyond being mother and son, they shared their loneliness.</t2634> <t2635>Pilar Ternera had lost all her hopes.</t2635> <t2636>She had forgotten the resonance of her laughter, which had turned into the heavy strokes of an organ, her breasts had been ruined by endless squeezes, and she had fallen victim to the inevitable fate of a woman whose belly and hips were shared.</t2636> <t2637>Yet, her heart had aged without hardening.</t2637> <t2638>She had become like a plump, talkative, self-indulgent maternal housewife, had cast aside the empty dreams of the cards, and had begun to find peace and solace in the loves of others.</t2638> <t2639>In the house where Aureliano Jose took his afternoon naps, the neighboring girls would meet with their lovers.</t2639> <t2640>After entering without question, they would say, -Pilar, can we use your room for a while?</t2640>
<t2641>Pilar would respond to them, "Of course, by all means," and if there was someone else at home, she would turn to them and explain, "I too am happy to know that people are happy in bed."</t2641>
<t2642>He wouldn't take any money in return for this service.</t2642> <t2643>Even in her old age, she never turned away men who came looking for her, without giving money, without giving love, and always without giving pleasure, nor did she ever turn away girls who wanted her room.</t2643> <t2644>All five of her daughters, each a legacy of a passionate seed, had grown up and gotten lost in the intricate paths of life.</t2644> <t2645>One of the two sons Pilar had raised and brought up had died fighting after joining Colonel Aureliano Buendia's forces, while the other had been caught and injured at the age of fourteen while trying to steal a crate of chicks from a village in the swamp.</t2645> <t2646>In a way, Aureliano Jose was the tall, dark man that the tarot priest had foretold for her half a century ago, and like all the men brought by the cards, he reached Pilar's heart after being marked by death on his forehead.</t2646> <t2647>The woman saw in the cards that he was destined for death.</t2647>
<t2648>"Don't go out tonight," he said.</t2648> <t2649>"Stay here."</t2649> <t2650>"Besides, Carmelita Montiel keeps begging me to put her in your arms."</t2650>
<t2651>Aureliano Jose could not grasp the hidden plea in those words.</t2651>
<t2652>-Tell her to wait for me at midnight, he said.</t2652>
<t2653>He went to the theater.</t2653> <t2654>A Spanish troupe was performing 'The Dagger of the Fox'.</t2654> <t2655>In fact, it was Zorrilla's play called The Dagger of the Goths.</t2655> <t2656>However, since the Liberals had nicknamed the Conservatives as Goths, Captain Aquiles Ricardo had changed the name of the play.</t2656> <t2657>Aureliano Jose only noticed that Captain Aquiles Ricardo and two soldiers with rifles were searching the audience after he went to the door and got his ticket.</t2657>
<t2658>Aureliano Jose, "Take it easy, captain."</t2658> <t2659>"No man born of a woman has dared to lay a hand on me," he said.</t2659> <t2660>The captain tried to search him by force, and the unarmed Aureliano Jose began to flee.</t2660> <t2661>The soldiers did not obey the order to shoot.</t2661> <t2662>One of them tried to explain, "He is a Buendia."</t2662> <t2663>Blinded by rage, the captain snatched the rifle from the soldier's hands, stood in the middle of the street, and took aim.</t2663> <t2664>"Cowards!" he shouted.</t2664> <t2665>"I wish it were Colonel Aureliano Buendia himself!"</t2665> <t2666>As the gunshot echoed, twenty-year-old untouched Carmelita Montiel, freshly bathed in orange blossom-scented water, was sprinkling rosemary leaves on Pilar Ternera's bed.</t2666>
<t2667>If it were up to Aureliano Jose, he would find the happiness Amaranta denied him in her.</t2667> <t2668>They would have exactly seven beautiful children.</t2668> <t2669>Aureliano Jose would spend many years with her and die of natural causes in her arms in his old age.</t2669> <t2670>However, the bullet that buried itself in his back and shattered his chest must have been fired due to a misinterpretation of the cards.</t2670> <t2671>According to the fortune, the one who was supposed to die that night was Captain Aquiles Ricardo, who indeed died four hours before Aureliano Jose.</t2671> <t2672>As soon as the gunshot was heard, the captain fell to the ground, hit by two bullets fired simultaneously from an unknown direction, and the night was interrupted by loud voices: "Long live the Liberal Party!"</t2672> <t2673>"Long live Colonel Aureliano Buendia!" At midnight, when Aureliano Jose died from blood loss and the fortune read for Carmelita Montiel proved false, a crowd of over four hundred gathered in front of the theater and emptied their pistols into the corpse of Captain Aquiles Ricardo, left in the middle of the street.</t2673> <t2674>His body, weighed down by the bullets and crumbling like soaked bread, was carried away by a patrolman with a wheelbarrow.</t2674>
<t2675>Annoyed by the excesses of career soldiers, General Jose Raquel Moncada used his political influence, donned his uniform again, and took control of the military and civil administration of Macondo.</t2675> <t2676>However, he hoped that his conciliatory attitude would prevent the inevitable.</t2676> <t2677>In September, various reports came in.</t2677> <t2678>While the government claimed to have control of the situation throughout the country, secret reports to the Liberals indicated armed uprisings in the interior.</t2678> <t2679>Those in power were reluctant to declare a state of war.</t2679> <t2680>However, following the court-martial decision that sentenced Colonel Aureliano Buendia to death in absentia, the situation was announced in a government communiqué.</t2680> <t2681>The first unit to capture the Colonel was ordered to execute the sentence.</t2681> <t2682>Ursula joyfully said to General Moncada, "This means he has returned."</t2682>
<t2683>However, Moncada had no knowledge of this matter.</t2683> <t2684>In fact, Colonel Aureliano Buendia had returned to the country more than a month ago.</t2684> <t2685>Before his arrival, various rumors had spread, claiming that the colonel was in several distant places at the same time, and even General Moncada did not believe he had returned until it was officially announced that he had captured two towns in the coastal region.</t2685> <t2686>Showing the telegram containing the official statement to Ursula, -Congratulations, dear friend.</t2686> <t2687>He will be here soon, he said.</t2687> <t2688>At that moment, Ursula became anxious for the first time.</t2688> <t2689>-What will you do? she asked.</t2689> <t2690>General Moncada had asked himself the same question many times.</t2690> <t2691>-I will do what he does, my friend, he said.</t2691> <t2692>I will fulfill my duty.</t2692>
<t2693>On the first of October, at dawn, Colonel Aureliano Buendia marched on Macondo with a thousand men, armed from head to toe.</t2693> <t2694>The garrison was ordered to hold out to the end.</t2694> <t2695>At noon, while General Moncada was having lunch with Ursula, a cannonball, whose rumble echoed throughout the town, shattered the facade of the treasury.</t2695>

<t2716>A kind of vitality connected to his inner coldness had protected him from aging and deteriorating.</t2716> <t2717>He was taller, paler, and bonier than when he had left, and had begun to show the first signs of resisting homesickness.</t2717> <t2718>Ursula thought to herself, -My God, he looks like someone who can do anything now, she said.</t2718> <t2719>Indeed, Aureliano Buendia had reached a point where he could do anything.</t2719> <t2720>The Aztec shawl he brought to Amaranta, the memories he recounted at dinner, the funny stories, were remnants of his former playful self.</t2720> <t2721>After the order to bury the dead in a common grave was carried out, Colonel Aureliano Buendia assigned Colonel Roque Carnicero to establish the court-martial.</t2721>

<t2849>This was perhaps the most critical moment of the war.</t2849> <t2850>The Liberal landowners, who had initially supported the revolution, had made secret agreements with the Conservative landowners to prevent the re-examination of land registry records.</t2850> <t2851>The exiled politicians who provided financial aid to the fighters announced to the public that all of Colonel Aureliano Buendia's powers had been taken away.</t2851> <t2852>But the colonel didn't care about authority at all.</t2852> <t2853>He never even picked up his poems, which filled five large notebooks and had been forgotten at the bottom of a chest.</t2853> <t2854>At night or when he took a nap, he would call one of the women to his hammock, and after reaching a superficial, primal satisfaction with her, he would collapse like a log and sleep.</t2854> <t2855>He was like a stone that neither sorrow nor worry ever touched.</t2855> <t2856>Only in those days did he know that he was doomed to struggle to the end with his heart turned into a tangled mess.</t2856> <t2857>Initially, he had been dizzy with the glorious air of his return and the considerable victories he had won, coming right to the edge of the abyss of greatness.</t2857> <t2858>With his animal hide clothing and tiger claw ornaments, the Duke of Marlborough, a great master of the art of war who terrified the young and was feared by the old, was Aureliano's right-hand man.</t2858> <t2859>He enjoyed having him constantly by his side.</t2859>

<t2932>The men looked at each other in astonishment.</t2932> <t2933>Colonel Aureliano Buendia held the ink pen in the air and unleashed the full weight of his authority on Colonel Gerinaldo Marquez.</t2933>

<t2935>Colonel Gerineldo Marquez stood up and placed his weapons on the table.</t2935>
<t2936>Colonel Aureliano Buendia said, "Go to the barracks and stand before the revolutionary court."</t2936>

<t2940>Two days later, Colonel Gerinaldo Marquez, who was being tried for treason, was sentenced to death.</t2940> <t2941>Colonel Aureliano Buendia was lying in his hammock, completely ignoring the pleas for Gerinaldo's pardon.</t2941> <t2942>On the night the sentence was to be carried out, Ursula, defying Aureliano's orders not to be disturbed, went to speak with him in his bedroom.</t2942> <t2943>Dressed in black from head to toe and looking unusually sorrowful as always, Ursula stood throughout the three-minute conversation with her son.</t2943> <t2944>Calmly, she said, "I know you are going to have Gerineldo shot."</t2944> <t2945>"I also know that there is nothing I can do to prevent it."</t2945> <t2946>"Still, I came to warn you: The moment I see Gerineldo's dead body, I swear on the bones of my dead father, on the bones of my dead mother, I swear on the memory of Jose Arcadio Buendia, I swear before God, that no matter what hole you crawl into, I will find you and kill you with my own hands."</t2946> <t2947>Without waiting for a response from Aureliano, Ursula turned and, before leaving through the door, concluded her words by saying, "Whether you have become like this or were born with a pig's tail, it's all the same."</t2947>
<t2948>Throughout that unending night, on one side, Colonel Gerineldo Marquez thought about the dead days spent in Amaranta's sewing room; on the other side, Colonel Aureliano Buendia struggled for hours to break through the hard shell of his loneliness.</t2948> <t2949>After that distant day when his father took him to see ice, his only happy moments were the times spent in his silver workshop making tiny fish.</t2949> <t2950>It had taken him thirty-two wars, breaking all his pacts with death, wallowing in the filth called fame like a pig, and losing exactly forty years to understand the superiority and privilege of simplicity.</t2950>
<t2951>At dawn, Colonel Aureliano Buendia, weary from a sleepless night spent in self-torment, entered the cell an hour before the execution.</t2951> <t2952>He said to Colonel Gerinaldo Marquez, The comedy is over, friend.</t2952> <t2953>-Let's get out of here before the mosquitoes carry out the death sentence.</t2953> <t2954>Colonel Gerinaldo Marquez couldn't hide his disgust at this attitude.</t2954>

<t2957>Colonel Aureliano Buendia said, "You won't see such a thing."</t2957> <t2958>"Now put on your shoes and help me end this damn war."</t2958>
<t2959>When Colonel Aureliano Buendia said these words, he did not know that starting a war was easier than ending one.</t2959> <t2960>He had to exert a full year of terrible and bloody effort to force the government to propose peace terms that the rebels would accept.</t2960> <t2961>He also had to spend another year convincing his own partisans that these terms were acceptable.</t2961> <t2962>He had to resort to unimaginable brutalities to suppress the uprising of his own officers who were unwilling to make peace and were pursuing absolute victory, and in the end, he hoped for help from enemy forces to make them give up.</t2962>
<t2963>He had never attained the stature of a great soldier as he did in those days.</t2963> <t2964>Knowing that he was fighting for his own salvation, rather than for abstract ideals or slogans that politicians would twist to their advantage, filled him with a fiery enthusiasm.</t2964> <t2965>Once having fought tirelessly for victory, now Colonel Gerineldo Marquez fought with faith and dedication for defeat, and he scolded Aureliano for recklessly endangering his life and not being cautious.</t2965> <t2966>Smiling, Aureliano said, "Don't worry."</t2966> <t2967>"Dying is much harder than it seems."</t2967> <t2968>For him, this was true.</t2968> <t2969>The belief that his death was predetermined gave him a mysterious immunity, a temporary immortality, allowing Aureliano to charge fearlessly into the most dangerous moments of battle.</t2969> <t2970>For this reason, he was able to achieve defeat, which was much harder, much bloodier, and much more costly than victory.</t2970>
<t2971>During the war that lasted almost twenty years, Colonel Aureliano Buendía had returned home many times.</t2971> <t2972>However, each time he came hurriedly, in between two important tasks, and his soldiers never left his side, creating an aura of legend around Aureliano that even Úrsula noticed.</t2972> <t2973>All of this eventually turned Aureliano into a stranger.</t2973> <t2974>When he opened a house for his three mistresses on his last visit to Macondo, he went to his own home only two or three times, just to call for meals.</t2974> <t2975>Beautiful Remedios and the twins, who were born during the war, knew him only from a distance.</t2975> <t2976>Amaranta, on the other hand, could not reconcile the memory of her brother, who had spent his youth making little goldfish, with this legendary warrior who kept a three-meter distance between himself and all of humanity.</t2976> <t2977>When the news of the ceasefire agreement spread, the household thought that Aureliano would finally be returned to his family, that he would come back to them as a human being once more, and they felt the family bonds that had been in the shadows for so long stronger than ever.</t2977>
<t2978>Ursula said, "Finally, there will be a man in our house again."</t2978>
<t2979>Amaranta was the first to sense that they had completely lost Aureliano.</t2979> <t2980>A week before the ceasefire agreement, Aureliano entered the house with two barefoot soldiers, without his officers and aides.</t2980> <t2981>The soldiers left the mule saddle and the chest containing the poems, which were all that remained of Aureliano's once-overflowing baggage, on the veranda.</t2981> <t2982>Amaranta called out to him as he passed in front of the sewing room.</t2982> <t2983>Colonel Aureliano Buendia did not recognize her.</t2983>
<t2984>Amaranta, in her joy at Aureliano's return home, said, "I am Amaranta," showing her hand wrapped in a black bandage.</t2984> <t2985>"Look."</t2985> <t2986>Colonel Aureliano Buendia smiled the same way he did that morning when he first saw the bandage on his sister's hand, having come to Macondo once condemned to death.</t2986>
<t2987>"How time flies," he said.</t2987> <t2988>"This is a terrible thing!"</t2988>
<t2989>The soldiers of the state had to protect the house.</t2989> <t2990>The people on the street were cursing and spitting at Aureliano, accusing him of needlessly igniting the war just to sell it at a better price in the end.</t2990> <t2991>Aureliano was shivering from both the heat and the cold.</t2991> <t2992>Wounds had opened up again under his armpits.</t2992> <t2993>Six months ago, when Ursula first heard the rumors of a ceasefire, she had opened the bridal room, cleaned it thoroughly, burned fragrant myrrh incense in every corner, and started waiting for her son to return home to slowly grow old among Remedios' now moldy dolls.</t2993>
<t2994>However, Aureliano had completed all his duties towards life, including aging, in the last two years.</t2994> <t2995>As he passed by the silver workshop that Ursula had meticulously prepared, Aureliano didn't even notice that the keys were in the lock.</t2995> <t2996>He didn't realize how time had gnawed at the house, made it decrepit, and brought about a situation that could be described as disastrous after so many years for someone who hadn't erased his memories from his mind.</t2996> <t2997>Neither the peeling plaster on the walls, nor the dirty, cotton-like cobwebs in the corners, nor the dust on the begonias, nor the worm-eaten beams, nor the rust covering the hinges caused Aureliano any pain; he didn't fall into any of the traps set by his longing for the house.</t2997> <t2998>He wrapped himself in his blanket, sat on the veranda, and watched the rain fall on the begonias all day.</t2998>
<t2999>As if he had come there only to wait for the rain to stop, he hadn't even taken off his boots.</t2999> <t3000>Ursula sensed that he wouldn't stay with them for long.</t3000> <t3001>-If he's not going to war anymore, then it means he will surely die, she thought.</t3001> <t3002>This assumption was so certain, so convincing that Ursula interpreted it as a prophecy.</t3002>
<t3003>That evening at dinner, Aureliano Segundo was tearing his bread with his right hand and eating his soup with his left hand.</t3003> <t3004>His twin brother Jose Arcadio Segundo, on the other hand, was tearing his bread with his left hand and eating his soup with his right hand.</t3004> <t3005>Their actions were so harmoniously synchronized that they looked more like someone playing in front of a mirror than two brothers sitting across from each other.</t3005> <t3006>This game, which they discovered when they realized they were identical twins, was repeated at dinner in honor of Aureliano's arrival.</t3006> <t3007>But Colonel Aureliano Buendia did not even notice.</t3007> <t3008>He was so detached and so disconnected from everything that he did not even see Beautiful Remedios passing by him naked as he went to the bedroom.</t3008> <t3009>Only Ursula dared to break his reverie.</t3009>
<t3010>Halfway through the meal, -If you have to leave again, at least try not to forget our situation tonight, he said.</t3010>
<t3011>Then Colonel Aureliano Buendia realized that the only person who could pierce through his pain and loneliness was Ursula.</t3011> <t3012>He wasn't surprised by this; for the first time in years, he looked at his mother's face.</t3012> <t3013>Ursula's skin had become like leather, her teeth had decayed, and her hair had lost its color.</t3013> <t3014>She had a frightening appearance.</t3014> <t3015>Aureliano compared his mother's appearance to his oldest memory of her, from the day she predicted that the boiling soup bowl would fall off the table, and found his mother shattered.</t3015> <t3016>He saw in an instant the traces, ulcers, wounds, and cracks that daily troubles over more than half a century had left on his mother, and realized that these did not evoke any feeling of pity in him.</t3016> <t3017>Then he made one last effort to find the place in his heart where emotions had rotted away, but he couldn't find it.</t3017>
<t3018>On another visit, when he sensed Ursula's scent on his own skin, he felt a feeling akin to shame, at the very least.</t3018> <t3019>Later, he noticed many times that Ursula's thoughts were mingling with his own.</t3019> <t3020>But the war had swept away all these feelings.</t3020> <t3021>Now even his wife Remedios was nothing more than a faint memory of someone who could be his daughter.</t3021> <t3022>The countless women he had known in the desert of love, and who had spread his seed throughout the coastal region, had left no trace in Aureliano's heart.</t3022> <t3023>Most of them had entered his room in the dark and left before dawn, leaving behind nothing but the fatigue in his body the next day.</t3023> <t3024>The only feeling that had endured without succumbing to time and war was the bond he had felt for his brother Jose Arcadio during their childhood.</t3024> <t3025>This, too, was a feeling based not on love, but on complicity.</t3025>
<t3026>Aureliano dismissed Ursula's request not to forget them by saying, "Forgive me, the war erased everything."</t3026> <t3027>In the days following that event, Aureliano busied himself with erasing all traces of his passage through the world.</t3027> <t3028>He distributed everything in the silver workshop until there was nothing left that was uniquely his.</t3028> <t3029>He gave his clothes to the soldiers.</t3029> <t3030>Feeling a guilt akin to what his father felt when he buried the spear that killed Prudencio Aguilar, he buried all his weapons in the yard.</t3030> <t3031>He kept only a pistol with a single bullet in it.</t3031> <t3032>Ursula did not interfere at all.</t3032> <t3033>Only when he attempted to destroy the picture of Remedios, illuminated by a lamp that burned day and night in the living room, did Ursula stop him.</t3033> <t3034>"This picture ceased to be yours long ago," she said.</t3034> <t3035>"It is now a family heirloom."</t3035> <t3036>On the night the armistice agreement came into effect, when there was nothing left in the house to remind anyone of him, Aureliano took the chest where the poems were kept and carried it to the kitchen, where Santa Sofia de la Piedad was preparing to light the oven.</t3036>
<t3037>Handing over a bundle of yellowed papers, he said, "Burn the oven with these."</t3037> <t3038>"They will burn better because they are very old."</t3038>
<t3039>Santa Sofia de la Piedad, that silent woman, that gentle, that woman who never conflicted with anyone, not even her own children, sensed that this was something that should not be done.</t3039>
<t3040>"These are important papers," he said.</t3040>
<t3041>The Colonel replied, "Not at all."</t3041> <t3042>"These are things a person scribbles to themselves."</t3042>
<t3043>-Then, come closer yourself, my colonel.</t3043>
<t3044>Aureliano not only threw the papers into the furnace with his own hands, but he also broke the chest into pieces with a cane axe and threw it into the fire.</t3044> <t3045>Hours earlier, Pilar Ternera had come to see him.</t3045> <t3046>Colonel Aureliano Buendia, after not seeing her for so many years, was surprised to see how the woman had aged, gained weight, and how her smile had lost its beauty, while at the same time he was astonished at how skillfully she had learned the language of the papers.</t3046> <t3047>Pilar had said to him, "Watch your mouth."</t3047> <t3048>Aureliano was pondering whether these words, once again spoken during his brightest days, had determined his fate to an astonishing degree.</t3048> <t3049>A short time later, while his private doctor was dressing his wounds, Aureliano, without seeming too interested, asked where exactly his heart was.</t3049> <t3050>The doctor listened with a stethoscope, then drew a circle on Aureliano's chest with a cotton swab dipped in tincture of iodine.</t3050>
<t3051>On the Tuesday morning when the weapons were laid down, a hot and rainy day dawned.</t3051> <t3052>Colonel Aureliano Buendia entered the kitchen before five o'clock and drank his usual plain coffee.</t3052> <t3053>Ursula said, "You were born on a day like this."</t3053> <t3054>"Everyone was astonished when you were born with your eyes open."</t3054> <t3055>Aureliano paid no attention to her stories because he was listening to the bugle sounds tearing through the dawn silence, the soldiers lining up, and the commands being given.</t3055> <t3056>After so many years of fighting, these sounds should not have felt unfamiliar, yet Aureliano felt the same weakness in his knees and the shiver in his skin that he had felt when he saw his first naked woman in his youth.</t3056> <t3057>He felt a strange longing, thinking that if he had married that woman, he would have been a happy, unknown artisan, unaware of war, fame, and glory.</t3057> <t3058>This unexpected shiver ruined his breakfast.</t3058> <t3059>At seven in the morning, when Colonel Gerineldo Marquez came to take him with a group of rebel officers, he found Aureliano more lonely, more withdrawn, and more pensive than ever.</t3059> <t3060>Ursula tried to throw a new cloak over Aureliano's shoulders.</t3060> <t3061>"What will the government say then?"</t3061> <t3062>"They'll think you surrendered because you didn't even have enough money to buy a cloak," she said.</t3062> <t3063>But Aureliano refused.</t3063> <t3064>As he was about to leave through the door, he put on Jose Arcadio Buendia's old felt hat at Ursula's insistence.</t3064>
<t3065>Ursula, said Aureliano.</t3065> <t3066>If you find yourself in trouble, in a difficult situation, promise me that in the last moment, you will think of your mother.</t3066>
<t3067>Aureliano raised his hand with fingers spread and smiled absentmindedly.</t3067> <t3068>Then, without saying a word, he left the house and plunged into the midst of curses, insults, and imprecations that pursued him until he was out of town.</t3068> <t3069>Ursula bolted the door with an iron bar, determined never to open it again until she died.</t3069> <t3070>"We will rot here," she thought.</t3070> <t3071>"We will turn to ashes in this manless house, but we will not give this vile town the pleasure of seeing us cry."</t3071>
<t3072>Ursula searched the house thoroughly all morning, looking in the most unlikely places, hoping to find a memento of her son.</t3072> <t3073>She found nothing.</t3073> <t3074>The signing ceremony took place twenty kilometers from Macondo, in the shade of a large tree around which the town of Neerlandia would later be established.</t3074> <t3075>Young seminarians, dressed in white and resembling a flock of doves startled by the rain, served the rebels who had laid down their arms, as well as the representatives of the government and the party.</t3075> <t3076>Colonel Aureliano Buendia arrived on a mule mired in mud.</t3076> <t3077>He had not shaved.</t3077> <t3078>He felt more pain from his wounds than from the shattering of his dreams.</t3078> <t3079>For he had reached the end of all hopes and had left behind his longing for fame and glory.</t3079> <t3080>In accordance with Aureliano's wishes, there were no bands playing, no bells ringing, no fireworks, no shouts of victory, nor any other displays that might alter the mournful nature of the truce.</t3080>
<t3081>The glass negatives of the photographer who managed to take the only remaining picture of Aureliano were shattered before the picture could be printed.</t3081> <t3082>The ceremony lasted only as long as it took to sign the documents.</t3082> <t3083>Around the wooden table in the middle of a patched-up fair tent sat the last officers loyal to Colonel Aureliano Buendia.</t3083> <t3084>Before the signatures were affixed, the President's special envoy wanted to read the surrender document aloud.</t3084>
<t3085>Colonel Aureliano Buendia objected to this.</t3085> <t3086>"Let's not waste time with formalities," he said, and prepared to sign the papers without reading them.</t3086> <t3087>Then one of his officers broke the lethargic silence in the tent.</t3087>
<t3088>-Colonel, please, for our sake, don't be the first to sign, he said.</t3088>
<t3089>Colonel Aureliano Buendia accepted this request.</t3089> <t3090>When the papers circled around the table in an absolute silence where the scratching of the pen on the paper was clear enough to distinguish the letters of the writings one by one, the signature space in the first row was empty.</t3090> <t3091>Colonel Aureliano Buendia prepared to fill that empty space.</t3091>
<t3092>Another of his officers interjected, "Colonel, there is still time for everything to be fixed," he said.</t3092>
<t3093>Colonel Aureliano Buendia, without changing the expression on his face, signed the first copy.</t3093> <t3094>As he was signing the last copy, a rebel colonel appeared at the door, pulling a mule loaded with two crates.</t3094> <t3095>Despite being very young, he had a dry, dull appearance and a patient demeanor.</t3095> <t3096>He was the treasurer of the revolutionary organization in the Macondo region.</t3096>
<t3097>For six days, he had trudged along the road with great difficulty, dragging a nearly dying mule to arrive just in time for the signing ceremony of the ceasefire.</t3097> <t3098>Reluctantly, with a heavy heart, he unloaded the crates, opened them, and laid out seventy-two gold bars one by one on the table.</t3098> <t3099>The existence of this fortune had slipped everyone's mind.</t3099> <t3100>In the chaos of the last year, when the command center had collapsed and the revolution had degenerated into a bloody power struggle among the leaders, it had become impossible to determine any responsibility.</t3100> <t3101>No one had paid attention to the revolutionary gold, which had been melted down, molded, and then covered with baked clay to look like bricks.</t3101> <t3102>Colonel Aureliano Buendia wrote down the seventy-two gold bars in the list of transferred items on the surrender document and ended the ceremony without giving anyone a chance to make a speech.</t3102> <t3103>The young man, dirty and grimy, stood before him, looking at him with his own dull, honey-colored eyes.</t3103>

<t3116>Aureliano Buendia had escaped the danger.</t3116> <t3117>The bullet had followed such a precise path that the doctor, after soaking a cloth in tincture of iodine, inserted it into Aureliano's chest and easily pulled it out from his back.</t3117> <t3118>Then, with a self-satisfied air, he said, "This was my masterpiece."</t3118> <t3119>"That was the only place where the bullet could pass without damaging any vital organs."</t3119> <t3120>Colonel Aureliano Buendia saw that he was surrounded by young priests murmuring desperate prayers for the salvation of his soul.</t3120> <t3121>It was then that he regretted not having shot the bullet into the roof of his mouth, as he had thought of doing, just to mock Pilar Ternera's prophecy.</t3121>
